Subject: [sfraves] BSP - Flaming Lotus Girls - in the RED - This Friday!

THIS Friday, December 5th 2008 7.00PM-6.00AM
Flaming Lotus Girls Presents:
In The Red!  Gallery Show and late night fundraiser

Burning Man is long past, and we're all dust free and have had
a chance to tally the books for Mutopia. Unfortunately, the
numbers are our favorite color, red. (this means we're up to
our lipsticked lips in debt.)

To help alleviate this, (and have some fun), we're throwing a
party THIS Friday, December 5th. 

We want to see all of our friends and family, so we're starting
the night early at 7pm with a cocktail party and gallery show-
come have a drink and enjoy stunning images of Mutopia.  There
will be a silent auction of framed photographs as well as the
usual Lotus Girl swag.  We will have a raffle with some lovely
prizes such as a burning man ticket and tickets to the
Edwardian Ball!!


The gallery show will wind down at 10, when we wind up the
sound system.

We've got a nice spot in lovely West Oakland, close to Bart,
bus lines and with ample parking.

Email info@flaminglotus.com for the address of the event or
call the info line day of event 415.963.3555

We'll be turning up the music at 10pm and keeping it going
until 6am. Come early, come late, stay later. For music we're
pulling in talent from all over the place. Local favorites from
Evil Breaks, Space Cowboys and others, and we're bringing in a
special treat from Budapest- one of Hungary's best
producer/DJs, Fine Cut Bodies. This will be the 4th time we've
brought him to SF- and you know that means he'll be providing
us with the sickest, most awesome beats you never knew about. 

7pm Gallery Show and Cocktail Party (Donation before 9.00PM)
10pm-6am Party!  $15 door, $10 presales and before 11.pm

Presale Tickets:
http://groovetickets.com/ordersystem/groove/eventviewqb.asp?AffilID=93&EventsID=43482&PGname=Evil%20Breaks

Info line for details: 415.963.3555

www.EvilBreaks.com
www.FlamingLotus.com

Subject: [sfraves] PUFUCHU SAYS- I'm Getting Too Old For This

--0-585433703-1228240061=:66873
Content-Type: text/plain; charset=us-ascii

yeah so maybe i've reached
the point where it's time to admit that i'm getting old and maybe i
should think about slowing down... it's not like i really have to be at
every party, not even most of them. it's not like i'm really going to
miss much of anything anyways right? 

OK. STEP AWAY FROM THE COMPUTER.

huh? what the fuck?

WHO ARE YOU AND WHAT HAVE YOU DONE WITH LAYLA?

dude,
pufuchu... calm down. i was just thinkin that i've been enjoying taking
it easy lately, not going out every weekend, sometimes only one night
instead of three....

OK THAT'S IT!!!

sorry
folks. i had to do it. seems like layla has gone and lost her damn
mind. i mean, she hasn't been out since Sting, and that's just not
right!!! so pufuchu is officially taking over. at least for this week.
cause it's her damn 30th birthday and if she doesn't do it in fine form
the world might just come to an end.... you're in good hands though....
i know how this thing works. 


WEDNESDAY DECEMBER 3RD

or Layla's 30th Birthday


yeah
that's right! you know that it's gonna be quite a weekend so you might
as well start early, right? seems only proper that layla should start
off the weekend that she thinks will be the last of her rockstar days
much as she started them, in as bassment rumblin to the sounds of
jungle!!! do you think she still has the skillz to keep space on the
dancefloor? there's only one way to find out.... 

p.s.-
it's actually her birthday.... though she might claim that every party
for the next two weeks is her birthday party, this is actually it....
you know what to do. 

THE POWER OF SOUND
Bossa Nova (in the Bassment)
8th @ Mission 
9pm-2am
$6-10 sliding scale

C-Los vs. Press Reset
Angst vs. Arson
Bass Ben vs. Ernie Trevino
Robin Weber vs. Frankie
Coopdville vs. Taso

hosted by MC Chronic G



THURSDAY DECEMBER 4TH


so
it seems that much of this week will be spent honoring long standing
traditions.... and on thursdays that can only mean one thing. no, not
hot chicks who love fishnets at delirium, though that was a fun
time...it's time to return to church! 

p.s.- it would serve layla right if adam dropped a country hop set... 

BEAT CHURCH
Shine 
Mission @ 9th
10pm-2am 
$5

AN-TEN-NAE
ANA SIA



FRIDAY DECEMBER 5th


thank
god layla's mom is gone! hopefully her visit was as sweet as it was
short, cause friday night is going to be a party and it's going to be
long. i can't confirm any rumors of bacon but if enough people believe
in it i bet it will come true, and we're all gonna need something to
keep us going at 6am cause it's been a while since EB has thrown a
proper party and you know what that means... 

p.s.-
so aaron went to burning man and i think he got seduced by hot girls
that like to play with fire and metal... so yes... this is also a
fundraiser for flaming lotus girls. but you love hot girls that play
with fire and metal too, so that works perfectly. besides, layla is
bartending at 4am. it's her birthday she'll get you drunk if she wants
too!

IN THE RED!!!!
info line: 415.963.3555
7pm-10pm: gallery show and cocktail party
10pm-6am: the real party happens!
$10-$15

SATURDAY DECEMBER 6TH


so
i've looked through all of layla's invites and various message boards
and even a couple websites. see, i thought after all of that it would
be obvious what layla was planning on for saturday night, and i have a
sneaking suspicion she thought she was going to enjoy a quiet
evening,.maybe a couple drinks with a few friends. but we all know
that's not going to happen. i could be wrong, but it looks like not
only EB is planning a return to its underground roots. it seems that if
layla were not temporarily insane there is only one thing she'd be
doing. 

p.s.- for the
love of god please! if by some twist of fate layla manages to regain
control of her body but has not fully regained her senses... i don't
know... find lucy or give her some whiskey or something!!! just make
sure she doesn't do something really dumb, like skip this party!!!

NIGHTMARE BEFORE CHRISTMAS
www.mallabelmusic.com for location

OWN

RIPPLE LABS

JAIME FUCKING COLE


i
can see that it's going to be quite a celebration, and though i know i
would thoroughly enjoy this weekend i do hope that layla comes to her
senses so she can properly celebrate her 30th birthday with all of you.
judging by the moments i've had to take control in the past there is
only one thing missing from the list so far.... perhaps it's in the
works, perhaps not... i'm sure if it hasn't happened by then a good
sunday session soakin up some sun and sippin champagne will set things
right! 

p.s.-
though i'm sure if she were speaking for herself she probably wouldn't
even mention sunday. but it would probably rock. i'm just sayin....

p.p.s.- peace love and beats- pufuchu

Subject: [sfraves] BSP: Monsta 005 out now - George Cochrane / The Fingermonsters / Andrew Phelan & Origami

Hi SFR peoples, wanted to share something with you that I'm really excited
about.  George has just released his debut solo dance music EP on Monsta
Music, and it's a brilliant one.  He's one of the most talented
musician/producer/people types I've ever met, let alone worked with, and
this release has been a long time coming.  Proud of you man!  On to the
spammage:

---

Monsta 005 - George Cochrane - Spencer Spiketail EP - Out Now!

For its fifth release, Monsta Music is proud to present the debut solo EP
from George Cochrane, aka Origami. Though his name may be new to the ears of
many, his music has been heard by the dance music community for years
through a variety of partnerships, including his work with DJ2, Andrew
Phelan & Origami, Cubik & Origami, and The Fingermonsters. The Spencer
Spiketail EP has been getting rave reviews, with a perfect 10/10 in iDJ,
comparisons to Green Velvet, Freaks, and Classic Recordings, and DJ support
from the likes of Satoshi Tomiie, Luke Solomon, Groove Armada, Laurent
Garnier, Johnny Fiasco, Onionz and M.A.N.D.Y. to name but a few.

1. My Synthesizer Won't Behave (Original Mix)
2. My Synthesizer Won't Behave (The Fingermonsters Mix)
3. My Synthesizer Won't Behave (Andrew Phelan & Origami Mix)

Available now at Beatport:

http://www.beatport.com/label/monsta+music

iDJ Perfect 10 Review:

"A wonderful name for a track is 'My Synthesizer Won't Behave'. And its
style - all rough jacking electro drums, bleeps, fat basslines and, most
memorably, Green Velvet-style vocals - lives up to its name.  The breakdown
is a a showstopper.  The fun doesn't end there. Andrew Phelan and Origami's
remix is a masterpiece of percussion power and, if anything, outdoes the
original. Monsta have a monster on their hands." - Jez Torrance

DJ Support: M.A.N.D.Y., Satoshi Tomiie, Luke Solomon, Onionz, Laurent
Garnier, Q-Burns Abstract Message, Johnny Fiasco, Tedd Patterson, Troydon,
Funky Transport, Sleazy McQueen.

Radio Support: Ministry of Sound, Kiss FM, Ibiza Global, Radio Fritz,
Proton, Chicago House FM, Ibizasonica, Top, Cyberjamz, Frisky,
Myhouse-Yourhouse.

Notable Quotables:

Satoshi Tomiie "Cool and nicely twisted.. feeling it:)"
Tom Findlay (Groove Armada) "Great vocal, perfect for those left of centre
nights"
Johnny Fiasco "some tech-filth-funk!!"
Onionz "FAT ASS BASS. DOPE DRUMS"
Tedd Patterson "Im really feelin this little ditty!"
Nathan Cole "Ablsolutely bloody marvelous and will play till the cows come
home and go back out again."
Funky Transport "cool EP! really liking this. full support!"
Sleazy McQueen "I love my synths cause they don't behave."

---

Worried about Monstas attacking you in the night? Eating you and your
children? Protect yourself with high quality Monsta Music apparel available
via Spread Shirt, currently featuring the exquisite Cornelius McFang and
Gilbert Slimejaw lines of urban combat fashion accessories.

http://192440.spreadshirt.com/us/US/Shop/

For more information on George Cochrane, Andrew Phelan & Origami, The
Fingermonsters and Monsta Music visit:

http://www.prismatictracks.com

SATURDAY DECEMBER 6TH


so
i've looked through all of layla's invites and various message boards
and even a couple websites. see, i thought after all of that it would
be obvious what layla was planning on for saturday night, and i have a
sneaking suspicion she thought she was going to enjoy a quiet
evening,.maybe a couple drinks with a few friends. but we all know
that's not going to happen. i could be wrong, but it looks like not
only EB is planning a return to its underground roots. it seems that if
layla were not temporarily insane there is only one thing she'd be
doing. 

p.s.- for the
love of god please! if by some twist of fate layla manages to regain
control of her body but has not fully regained her senses... i don't
know... find lucy or give her some whiskey or something!!! just make
sure she doesn't do something really dumb, like skip this party!!!

would thoroughly enjoy this weekend i do hope that layla comes to her
senses so she can properly celebrate her 30th birthday with all of you.

works, perhaps not... i'm sure if it hasn't happened by then a good
sunday session soakin up some sun and sippin champagne will set things
right!

even mention sunday. but it would probably rock. i'm just sayin....

Ok - admittedly=2C this one is pretty damn ill content-wise - but TSOL (aka=
 True Sounds of Liberty) were more SoCal punk pioneers=2C and Jack (the sin=
ger) has a reputation for being a sick=2C twisted fucker. I think these lyr=
ics prove that point...

"Code Blue" by TSOL=20

I never got along with the girls at my school

Filling me up with all their morals and their rules

They'd pile all their problems on my head

I'd rather go out and fuck the dead

'Cause I can do what I want and they won't complain

I wanna fuck I wanna fuck the dead

Middle of the night so silently

I creep on over to the mortuary

Lift up the casket and fiddle with the dead

Their cold blue flesh makes me turn red

'Cause I can do what I want and they won't complain

I wanna fuck I wanna fuck the dead

And I don't even care how she died...

But I like it better if she smells  of formaldehyde!

Never on the rag or say leave me alone

They don't scream and they don't moan

Don't even cry if I shoot in their hair

Lying on the table she smiles and she stares

After a couple months of intense techno, we are pleased to present one for
the house heads!

If you dig that tasteful, groovy minimal house we so enjoyed from Dan Bell,
you will be in for a treat, as Cassy plays in a fairly similar style.

Check out the September 08 mix below for a nice taste of what you're in for.

Monocle are extremely talented as well, and have barely left their houses in
the last month, preparing an all new live set just for this show.

Great shit. Really excited for this one!

Hope to see some SFR folks out. :)

---->GB

____________________________________________________


Saturday, December 6th, 2008

[ K O N T R O L ]

minimal techno + avant house
every 1st Saturday at The Endup



featuring from Berlin:

CASSY  - 3 hour DJ set

(panoramabar . perlon . uzuri . m_nus)
(playhouse . dessous . mental groove)

After growing up a musically-oriented child in London and
Vienna, Cassy Britton moved to Berlin in 2003 to pursue a
full time career in music and hasn't looked back.  In the
years since, she has produced two EPs for Perlon,
founded her own "Cassy" label, landed a residence at
Berlin's famed Panoramabar (also mixing their first ever
compilation), and collaborated with the likes of Ricardo
Villalobos, Luciano, Mathew Jonson, Steve Bug, and
Swayzak. Known for her smooth and soulful fusing of deep
house and minimal grooves, we are excited and honored to
introduce Cassy to SF with a 3 hour (100% vinyl!) West
Coast debut set.



plus special guests:

MONOCLE - Live PA

(racecar productions . nightlight music)

Monocle is the collaborative live project of Christina
Chatfield and Danny Patterson, two award-winning sound
designers that met while studying music technology at
the prestigious Berklee College of Music. Upon graduating
they relocated to SF, where they continue to write music
and perform together, and have produced tracks for
Racecar Productions and Alland's own Nightlight Music.
After a few months in hiding, they are pleased to debut an
all new live set for [KONTROL] that is sure to turn heads.



with [KONTROL] residents:

ALLAND BYALLO  (nightlight . auralism . leibe*detail)
SAMMY D  (dirtybird . utensil . magnificent 7)
NIKOLA BAYTALA  (s.w.a.t. . robsoul . junior boys own)
CRAIG KUNA  (platform . esdjco)


____________________________________________________

401 6th St @ Harrison, SF
10pm - 6am / 21+ / $15 til 2am
http://www.theendup.com

FREE before 11pm!

http://www.kontrolsf.com/K42/K42P.jpg


___________________________________________________


CASSY

Catherine Britton aka Cassy left England for Austria with her Caribbean
father and Austrian mother in 1975. She spent her childhood in Vienna and
Lower Austria learning to sing and studying music at an early age. After
studying drama and acting in London for three years she returned to her
hometown of Vienna and began working in the theatre. But she soon gave up
acting when she realised she couldn't stand the profession.

Her first professional step into the electronic music world was as a
vocalist for Elin aka Autorepeat on 'Music Takes Me Higher' on Sabotage
Records. Electric Indigo was able to convince Cassy to not only involve
herself as a singer but to learn how to mix records.

After her first DJ gigs in Vienna, Munich and further productions, she met
Dave the Hustler in Geneva where they started working on a collaborative
project for Mental Groove, Cassy & Dave the Hustler. Geneva was also where
she met Luciano, co-producing 'La Ondita' on his album 'Blind Behaviour'.
She also co-produced 'Alpine Rocket' with Mathew Jonson for Perlon.

With her move to Berlin in March 2003, inspired by the clubscene and the
numerous number of artists living there and the abundance of the music she
fell in love with, she started becoming increasingly active in Berlin's club
scene and shortly after, became involved in projects with artists such as
Steve Bug and Ricardo Villalobos. She also started her solo project,
producing and singing.

Since then, she has founded her own label, "Cassy", where she will be
concentrating on releasing her own music, and she has recently finished her
first mix compilation for Berlin's Panoramabar, her club residency.

MONOCLE

Monocle is a collaboration between two award-winning sound designers,
Christina Chatfield and Danny Patterson. The duo first met at the Berklee
College of Music in Boston, Massachusetts where they both studied music
technology. What began as a collaboration for class blossomed into a
full-fledged live PA and production team.

Originally from the Midwest, Christina's musical tastes were heavily
influenced by the sounds of nearby Detroit and Chicago. After spending her
teenage years at various electronic music events, she knew she wanted to
take her interest in the music to a higher level. With several years of
classical music training under her belt and a lifelong fascination with
sound design, Christina began studying music synthesis at Berklee in 2004.
In 2006 she was the recipient of the Laurie Anderson Women in Music
Technology award for her outstanding work at the college. In addition to
developing her many music projects--which include her solo productions as
Anitserk and collaborations with other artists in the works--Christina
produces sound design for visual media.

Danny hails from northern Florida where he was surrounded by computers since
early childhood. He began working with electronic music production as early
as 13 years old and hasn't stopped since. Danny's impressive resume already
boasts music production credits for his work on an Academy Award-winning
film and a top-selling Playstation game. Having previously studied computer
science, Danny is also a skilled programmer, often turning to programming
platforms like Supercollider and Composers Desktop Project to further create
and manipulate sound. In addition to working on his solo techno debut as
Coupler, Danny is currently putting his programming talents to use as a
software engineer developing music applications.

Monocle's debut release Dilleniidae (May 2007, Racecar Productions) was an
immediate success, drawing praise and plays from high-profile corners.
Shortly after its release, Dilleniidae appeared on several minimal download
charts, climbing to number 2 on Dance Tracks Digital and securing a place in
the top 40 on Juno Records.

Monocle's tracks expose listeners to a diverse spectrum of beats, ranging
anywhere from dark minimalist soundscapes to thoughtful analog melodies with
a groove. Both producers interject their own unique sound while effortlessly
blending together, resulting in dance music that conveys a deep
understanding of production and composition.


===> LINKS:

http://www.myspace.com/monoclemusik

Monocle's Website:
http://www.monocle-music.com/

HBC presents:

Molekle : an entity of strongly connected components, each with well defined individual properties, yet the synthesized entity possesses properties unique to itself.

Friday, 5 December 2008

BANGING:
ALIXR: Pulse|FnF [SF]
ROBOTHEAD: Faktion|Heroic Robot [ SF ]
KIRILL: Molekle|Key9sound [ SF ]
visuals by HEROIC ROBOT

CHILLING:
MARCO (miss gawker): SPaz [ SF ]
DISCONNECT: DEF| Molekle [ SF ]
DJ HEROIC: Faktion|Heroic Robot [ SF ]

ALIXR aka Alex, is known for curing dancefloors of lethargy and boredom with his intuitive track selection, seamless mixing style, and high-energy enthusiasm behind the decks.  In the recent years he's been spinning, Alixr has played such high-profile events as San Francisco's How Weird Street Faire and Southern California's legendary Moontribe full moon desert gatherings.

ROBOTHEAD: Like his native Philly, Robothead packs his sets with meaty layers of danceable music.  Equally at home spinning House and Techno, this versatile DJ is also making a name for himself in the hot SF visualist team Heroic Robot.  Call this description cheesy, but you know you like it, just like the sandwich.

KIRILL was born in Uzbekistan and grew up on various styles of electronica. Having touched his first set of decks nearly 11 years ago, he continues to explore his interest in music and to share his findings with people through technology. Having performed at many underground events while earning a solid rep as a DJ, Kirill is ready to bring his choice of sound to you.

MARCO has long been a pioneer of the strange, obscure and the bizarre, as an explorer in the audio and video realms he has brought noize, beats, and visualizations to many an event, underground & above ground. you can catch him DJing/VJing (as missgawker) somewhere about town, or playing his own original beats at out-of-the way venues around the bay area or on the globe somewhere, being an ongoing student of subcultures and countercultures around the world....his desire never stops....

DISCONNECT, known widely as a techno DJ who spins a dreamy, groovin' laid back style with a dash of progressive and Neo Detroit thrown in, also spins real electro.  He has been throwing underground parties with the DEF crew since 2003, and is known for his depth and breadth of knowledge of all things EDM.

DJ HEROIC presents chilled IDM and liquid helium ambient from the mind that brought you Heroic Robot's brain-twisting visuals.



Julie's Supperclub
1123 Folsom Street (near 7th St across from BrainWash), San Francisco, CA
9 PM to 2 AM 21+
Cost: $5 after 10pm

MARCO has long been a pioneer of the strange, obscure and the bizarre, as an explorer in the audio and video realms he has brought noize, beats, and visualizations to many an event, underground & above ground. you can catch him DJing/VJing (as missgawker) somewhere about town, or playing his own original beats at out-of-the way venues around the bay area or on the globe somewhere, being an ongoing student of subcultures and countercultures around the world....his desire never stops....

DISCONNECT, known widely as a techno DJ who spins a dreamy, groovin' laid back style with a dash of progressive and Neo Detroit thrown in, also spins real electro.  He has been throwing underground parties with the DEF crew since 2003, and is known for his depth and breadth of knowledge of all things EDM.

DJ HEROIC presents chilled IDM and liquid helium ambient from the mind that brought you Heroic Robot's brain-twisting visuals.



Julie's Supperclub
1123 Folsom Street (near 7th St across from BrainWash), San Francisco, CA
9 PM to 2 AM 21+
Cost: $5 after 10pm

gear, and otherwise make sure HR is able to kick ass. :)

Just need a better comic book name than Laser Ray ;)

Hope you enjoyed the broadcast, party sounded pretty darn awesome from
where we were. :)

-R.

> ALIXR aka Alex, is known for curing dancefloors of lethargy and boredom with his intuitive track selection, seamless mixing style, and high-energy enthusiasm behind the decks. In the recent years he's been spinning, Alixr has played such high-profile events as San Francisco's How Weird Street Faire and Southern California's legendary Moontribe full moon desert gatherings.
> 
> ROBOTHEAD: Like his native Philly, Robothead packs his sets with meaty layers of danceable music. Equally at home spinning House and Techno, this versatile DJ is also making a name for himself in the hot SF visualist team Heroic Robot. Call this description cheesy, but you know you like it, just like the sandwich.
> 
> KIRILL was born in Uzbekistan and grew up on various styles of electronica. Having touched his first set of decks nearly 11 years ago, he continues to explore his interest in music and to share his findings with people through technology. Having performed at many underground events while earning a solid rep as a DJ, Kirill is ready to bring his choice of sound to you.
> 
> MARCO has long been a pioneer of the strange, obscure and the bizarre, as an explorer in the audio and video realms he has brought noize, beats, and visualizations to many an event, underground & above ground. you can catch him DJing/VJing (as missgawker) somewhere about town, or playing his own original beats at out-of-the way venues around the bay area or on the globe somewhere, being an ongoing student of subcultures and countercultures around the world....his desire never stops....
> 
> DISCONNECT, known widely as a techno DJ who spins a dreamy, groovin' laid back style with a dash of progressive and Neo Detroit thrown in, also spins real electro. He has been throwing underground parties with the DEF crew since 2003, and is known for his depth and breadth of knowledge of all things EDM.
> 
> DJ HEROIC presents chilled IDM and liquid helium ambient from the mind that brought you Heroic Robot's brain-twisting visuals.

Tonal, the Bay Area's favorite underground event, returns for its holiday
bash with a sinister lineup befitting of this installation's mascot: The
Grinch.  The Mayor of Tonal-ville recently issued an All Points Bulletin
searching for this vile green creature after getting wind that he was
pulling down mistletoe, unplugging sound systems, and stealing booze from
all of the local parties.  Intelligence reports from the TIA (Tonal
Investigative Agency) suggest that Mister Grinch will be captured this
December 13th.  In the meantime please report any nefarious activity
perpetrated by green monstrosities to the underground authorities, and get
ready to join the rest of Tonal-ville as we invade the East Bay for the
first time!

Thanks to all who made it out for Cassy and Monocle on Saturday. What

[KONTROL] parties at The Endup. :)

is teaming up with Mezzanine to present Demon Days, the traveling
party hosted and headlined by Detroit Techno legend Carl Craig!!!

Ask anybody who saw Carl Craig's live set at DEMF this year about it
and just watch their eyes glass over and the goosebumps raise on their
arms. Yes, it really was THAT good.

I was lucky enough to also catch Carl's headlining set at this year's
Decibel festival just a couple months ago, and again he blew me away,
this time behind the decks. This is a guy who knows how to take the
art and artistry of techno to that next level. A true showman and a
true professional.

We are all very excited and honored to be a part of the SF version of
Demon Days for the second year in a row.

Carl f***ing Craig, people.

Respect.

i know that i live in a temporal anomaly where a day is often 72 hours
but i didn't realize how warped it was until i was talking to a friend
at my birthday party on friday. i suppose normally there is only a week
between my birthday and new year's eve because normally my birthday
lasts from thanksgiving until white christmas but my birthday is over,
so this is going to be one very long week, and there is a lot going on!
and talk about temporal anomalies!!!! the mk36 broadcast signal has
finally made it back to earth after getting lost in a wormhole, just in
time for space invader's birthday! to preserve my dimensions timeline
and my sanity i'm going to think of this as friday, but for the rest of
you...



THURSDAY Dec. 11th


which, come to think of it, is my little sister's birthday. i
should send her something. at least an e-mail. but more importantly, do
any of you guys remember this party called eklectik hektic? some of you
might still frequent the groundscore message board, but=A0 for those of
you who have no clue what i'm talking about.... when i moved here 5
years ago there was this crew groundscore. they ran the dnb (and
pre-pubescent punk band) stage at haight street fair and threw these
awesome dnb/breaks parties called eklectik hektic. anyways, i vaguely
remember this dj felix tha dog. i think he must have eaten the housecat
cause this guy was fuckin wikkid! and he's back! and playing tonight at
mixtape....=20

p.s. - it's Mace's birthday too!

MIXTAPE
Shine=20
Mission @ 9th
10pm-2am=20
$5=20

FELIX THA DOG
ALEX WINDSOR
MACE
WALKER



FRIDAY Dec. 12th


"sunny days! sweepin the clouds away! on my way to where the air is sweet!!=
!""=20

the
temporal anomalies continue! i've been singing this song to myself a
lot lately.... trying to remember what the world looked like to me when
i was a young girl. i wish i could say that i can clearly see the
images, but i can't. which is why i'm not one of the artists presenting
a vision of childhood utopia... or dystopia, at the goforaloop gallery
on friday night. but i am happy to be helping them raise money for
DrawBridge, a local organization providing art programs to homeless and
vulnerable children in the bay area. what better way to spend an
evening than enjoying good art and music!=20

t'is the season! but fuck santa, tonight it's all about the elves,

worry about his list, and tonight you won't have to either! come be as
naughty as you want!

From: "electrofunk138@hotmail.com" <electrofunk138@hotmail.com>
To: SF Raves <sfraves@hyperreal.org>

Subject: [sfraves] SRR: So long and thanks for all the fish....



Hey SFR - 

I have been trying to figure out how to say this...how to express myself without sounding too bitter or depressed or whatever, but maybe short and to the point is just the best way. 

The last few weeks for me have been really shitty. I don't want to get into details or be all gossipy or dramatic, but suffice it to say, it's just simply my time to bow out of this scene. I have met some truly good people in my time here, and I sincerely hope to stay in touch with and remain friends with you folks. I have also met some people who will smile in your face and call you friend while they talk shit behind your back, fuck you over, and in general, the type of individuals that make a human want to pick up a rifle and go all "charles whitman" on folks. (not to say this doesn't occur outside of the rave scene, but it just seems to have been worse in my personal experience) 

Anyway - this weekend I have reached my breaking point, and I am done. 

That being said - I'm unsubbing after this post, and anyone who would like to keep in contact, just save my email addy or ping my cell. If you want my contact info, ask and ye shall receive. 

Now on to the bright side (for someone)....

I'm also hanging up DJing...so all my remaining vinyl (about 5 or 6 crates worth at least) is up for sale. It ranges from old school Sasha & Digweed era trance, to tech-house, breaks, tech-funk, drumNbass, etc. If anyone wants the whole shebang, I'll work out a deal with you. There's probably about $2000 or more in worth, but I'd settle for $500 for the whole lot. You could sell a small portion of that on eBay and more than make your money back. I also have a bazillion digital files...ok, maybe more like 4000, but, if you want them, I'll swap 'em for $$ or herb or something. My digi-tunes are more breakbeat, tech-funk, techno, minimal, tech-house and drumNbass....

Anyhoo...I wish everyone the best, and I hope everyone has a safe and happy holiday. I'm off to reprioritize my life and get my head straight...

It's been a ride....

Catch you on the flipside
Marco

----- Message from <electrofunk138@hotmail.com> on Mon, 15 Dec 2008 
11:47:17 -0800 -----
To:
SF Raves <sfraves@hyperreal.org>
Subject:
SRR: So long and thanks for all the fish....


Hey SFR - 

I have been trying to figure out how to say this...how to express myself 
without sounding too bitter or depressed or whatever, but maybe short and 
to the point is just the best way. 

The last few weeks for me have been really shitty. I don't want to get 
into details or be all gossipy or dramatic, but suffice it to say, it's 
just simply my time to bow out of this scene. I have met some truly good 
people in my time here, and I sincerely hope to stay in touch with and 
remain friends with you folks. I have also met some people who will smile 
in your face and call you friend while they talk shit behind your back, 
fuck you over, and in general, the type of individuals that make a human 
want to pick up a rifle and go all "charles whitman" on folks. (not to say 
this doesn't occur outside of the rave scene, but it just seems to have 
been worse in my personal experience) 

Anyway - this weekend I have reached my breaking point, and I am done. 

That being said - I'm unsubbing after this post, and anyone who would like 
to keep in contact, just save my email addy or ping my cell. If you want 
my contact info, ask and ye shall receive. 

Now on to the bright side (for someone)....

I'm also hanging up DJing...so all my remaining vinyl (about 5 or 6 crates 
worth at least) is up for sale. It ranges from old school Sasha & Digweed 
era trance, to tech-house, breaks, tech-funk, drumNbass, etc. If anyone 
wants the whole shebang, I'll work out a deal with you. There's probably 
about $2000 or more in worth, but I'd settle for $500 for the whole lot. 
You could sell a small portion of that on eBay and more than make your 
money back. I also have a bazillion digital files...ok, maybe more like 
4000, but, if you want them, I'll swap 'em for $$ or herb or something. My 
digi-tunes are more breakbeat, tech-funk, techno, minimal, tech-house and 
drumNbass....

Anyhoo...I wish everyone the best, and I hope everyone has a safe and 
happy holiday. I'm off to reprioritize my life and get my head straight...

It's been a ride....

Catch you on the flipside
Marco


--=_alternative 0014631385257521_=--

their annual Fire and Electricity Spewing White Holly in the 2008 
Sausalito Yacht Club's "Parade of Lights" on San Francisco Bay.  This 
year marked the addition of The White Holly with a tesla coil hanging of 
the side and fire spewing art topside.

I am sure some of you were there...  I can't remember any of the names of the parties, but I was there for a good majority of 'em.

Michael Liu gave me one of his tapes there.

DJ Moda threw out two CDS and I caught both (threw the second one back into the crowd).

DJ Hobbit gave me his tape (what happened to that kid?)

Met Pistachio & Anonymous and asked if I could pass out flyers for them (never followed through)

Anyone remember the "Sam the Butcher" paintings? REALLY CREEPY depending on your influence.

Gettin freaky in the loft with candy girls holding stuffed animals.

Accidentally punching a girl in the face while giving her a light show (oops)

During one party the cops ran in and shut down the place, those of us who were fortunate enough to be in the back room shut the doors and the music and kept quiet until they left.  We then proceeded to party till morning, so dope!

Subject: Re: [sfraves] Oakland Crackhouse Memories


On Wed, 17 Dec 2008, fable wrote:
-&e->I am sure some of you were there...  I can't remember any of the 
-&e->names of the parties, but I was there for a good majority of 'em.

Hey Fable, long time no hear!

So the back story on that building:

I used to do sound there for probably half the parties there for about a 
year or so.  DJ'd a lot there too.  It was funny, people would book me 
half because I had a decent sound system and didn't charge much (and would 
play for free if I did sound, I mena I'm there already, right?), and half 
because I was one of the only people in the rave scene who got along well 
with the older afro-american gent by the name of Wesley Robinson (known to 
most as Wes) who ran the back room and actually booked the parties.  He 
and I would kick it often in the later hours of parties and talk about the 
Black Panthers, some of his social interactions with the kings of bebop 
jazz, the wheel inside the wheel, Peter Tosh, why the rave scene would 
never be able to spark a revolution in America, and how badly a night of 
nothing but trance sucks.  Just a seriously _real_ DIY ethic guy who had 
lived through some amazing times.

Had a lot of really fun times, some of the most vibe soaked raves went 
down there, but one night the main group I did parties with just 
mismanaged things so badly I had to get out of doing parties there.  
Suffice to say one of the promoters freaked out over an admittedly tough 
situation at the door and almost got his gun (wtf, why is it the more day 
glo colors on a flyer, and the more they talk about plur the more likely 
they pack heat?).  This is um, pretty much never a good idea in that 
little part of West Oakland.

It continued to be used for parties in this 4 month cycle, until it would 
get busted, cool down for a month or two and start back up again.  I sorta 
lost touch with it after just plain too many cars got broken into and too 
much shady shit.

Enter several years later, a friend of mine tells me he has a rehearsal 
space he wants to split in Oakland.  We get there and WTF, it's the same 
place.

We had regular band practice there for about two years till a chain of 
events a few months ago forced us to move (it's hard to leave a rented 
room measuring about 20x15 for $350 a month).  First off, the place was 
just crawling with methheads that either lived there or would stop by 
(strangely, most of the bands that practiced there would show up for 
practice and just leave when done, ducking this whole world).  Most of 
them were nice people most of the time, but alas, that substance does not 
lend itself to consistently rational behavior and a feeling of 
togetherness.  It seemed the only person who was a stabilizing persona 
there was Wes.  He was grumpy, hated electronic music, and lived for jazz, 
and bands like Bad Brains and 24/7 Spyz.  Wes had been an active promoter 
of top shelf music usually featuring black artists, even booking Bad 
Brains for their first west coast gigs.  Sadly, Wes passed away shortly 
after we moved my band in (I think he was in his late 70s).  More and more 
people it seemed were living there (it was supposed to be just a music 
rehearsal studio).  Shady shit was overflowing, when one of the tennants 
was found to be in alleged possession of a few pounds of herb, intent to 
sell, etc.  Of all the weird shit that happened there, it's laughable that 
the thing that finally does them in is a half trashbag of doja.

We were told a bit after that, that eviction was emminent, all tennants 
had to be out by August 1st of this year.  We figured we didn't want to be 
there another second so we beat the deadline by a fair bit.

A couple days later three men armed with pistols broke into one of the 
rooms in the building, pistol whipped everybody present and beat the 
living shit out of a former guitarist for Exodus.  If I'm not mistaken he 
now has permanent damage to one eye.

Part of the fun of that place was the sense of urban decay and 
impermanence that sorta helps that "this moment is magic" you only get at 
a underground held at a sketchy location.  Too bad it really was that 
sketchy, if not more.

As for what parties were done there (memory is a bit hazy as this is 
pushing a decade back)... but Harmony, First Light, Warmth, Children of 
the Sun, ASR, Happy Kids, Skills and T&J factory I think all threw events 
there.  Bands that had rehearsed there include Sam the Butcher, Mommy's 
Friend, Closer to the Real (who famously used a prisoner transfer bus as 
their tourbus), Testament, Exodus, Control-R, Skiffington, All Time Highs, 
Mad at Sam, and The Lag.

Probably one of the great fire code nightmare renegade rave spaces of the 
SF rave scene, along with 115 Minna, the Acme, Tenderloft, the original 
Overworld, Cyborganic, the first dance studio space above the chinese 
food/donut shop on Mission... forever changed by some of those nights for 
sure.

The Sam the Butcher artwork, and the huge wall of messages to the late 
Paul Baloff (lead singer of exodus who died a few years back) were still 
there.  Last I heard the building is slated to be torn down and 
redeveloped by it's owner.

Rest in Peace 832 E. 11th.
andy

p.s.	you can google map/street view it @
http://maps.google.com/maps?f=q&source=s_q&view=text&q=836+E.+11th+oakland+ca&btnG=Search+Maps

Subject: [sfraves] BSP: Alpha Beats 1/23/09 feat. Doc Martin / Sunshine Jones / Jeno / Syd Gris + more!

Friday, January 23rd

Rock It Science and Prismatic present:

Alpha Beats: A is for Alien

The creators of Tonal, SF's highly acclaimed color themed warehouse party
series, take you to the next level with Alpha Beats.  Combining their knack
for booking insanely diverse and exciting lineups, bringing together a
killer crowd that goes berzerk on the dance floor, transforming spaces into
themed experiences, and building a party that goes way beyond one night,
Rock It Science and Prismatic invite you to experience the launch of their
new event series Alpha Beats.  For the letter A, Alpha Beats brings you an
outer worldly Alien experience at DNA Lounge, taking you to Outer Space with
some of the West Coast's most influential pioneers and to Inner Space with
front edge trail blazers of the next generation. 

Outer Space:

DOC MARTIN (Sublevel, LA)

One of the world's favorite DJs, Doc Martin hardly needs an introduction.
Beginning his mission on the decks back in the summer of 1986, his focus on
house music from the land of funk and disco was triggered while playing the
club and warehouse scene in San Francisco during the late '80s and 90's. As
one of the major players in laying the foundations of a strong West Coast
dance scene, Doc has always been a master of mixing the crowd with the
music.

SUNSHINE JONES (King Street, Treehouse Muzique, Sunday Soul, Imperial Dub,
Dubtribe Sound System)

Founding member of Dubtribe Sound System, producer of classics such as "Do
It Now" and "Mother Earth" for labels like Guidance, King Street, Defected,
and Imperial DUB, Sunshine Jones continues to pioneer, produce, and perform
live/DJ sets all over the world.  His passion for improvisation, dance, and
devotion to deepness send him and his dance floors out among the stars
forever.

JENO (Back2Back, Noise From the Void)

After heading to San Francisco in the early 90's, Jeno began the now
legendary 'Full Moon' parties with the infamous Wicked crew. The friendly
vibe and hedonistic atmosphere found at these free outdoor events attracted
a large and diverse crowd of people, setting the tone for the future of the
electronic dance music scene in Northern California.  He has now become one
of most loved and sought after dj's in the United States.

Drums by Xavier (Remedy)

Inner Space:

SYD GRIS (Opel, Opulent Temple)

Syd Gris has been called a Renaissance man of the West Coast scene, and with
good reason.  Founding Opel Productions, Opulent Temple, and being heavily
involved in SF's Lovefest event are merely the tip of the ice berg; Syd is
one of the West Coast's top talents, consistently being voted in the Top 10
San Francisco Dream Team poll, and playing the biggest events in California.

ERIC SHARP (Rock It Science, Flavor Group)

Eric Sharp's ascent to the forefront of dance music can only be described as
meteoric. From working countless dance floors into frenzies at clubs, bars,
and parties across the US and the globe to producing some of San Francisco's
most epic parties with his crew (and soon to be music label) Rock It
Science, Eric's seemingly endless energy and dedication to electronic music
is simply contagious.

THE FINGERMONSTERS (Monsta Music)

The Fingermonsters consist of Andrew Phelan, George Cochrane, Cubik, and
Shawn Allen.  Their production and Monsta Music label has been creating
quite a buzz recently, garnering support from some of the biggest DJs in the
world.   Their live PA is a site to behold, with all four members freaking
out together onstage on a variety of synths, drum machines, laptops, and
general insanity.

21+
10PM-4AM

$15 limited early bird presale
$20 regular presale and before 11:30
$25 after 11:30

Presales @ going.com/alphabeatsa

Free DJ mix for dressing in alien attire

DNA Lounge
375 Eleventh Street
Between Folsom & Harrison
www.dnalounge.com

www.rockitsciencesf.com
www.prismatictracks.com

Subject: [sfraves] NSFRR - Confessions of a Berghain junkie

------=_Part_36910_15719589.1229880034866
Content-Type: text/plain; charset=ISO-8859-1
Content-Transfer-Encoding: 7bit
Content-Disposition: inline

Happy solstice ravers . . .

Here in Berlin, it's bitterly cold and dark, and the renegades and open air
parties are dwindling. The outdoor afterhour clubs are closed for their
winter break. Not to say that things are quiet - there are still places to
go after 7am, just maybe more like 10 regular clubs instead of 100 scattered
parties.

During the Autumn and Winter seasons, I find myself at Berghain/Panorama Bar
almost every weekend. Living a 10 minute bike ride from one of the best
sound systems in the world, housed in a massive, gorgeous concrete building,
it's pretty hard to stay away. I know the place turns a lot of people off,
especially naive tourists who will inevitably get turned away by the nasty
and intimidating door man, or visitors not expecting the masses of muscular
dudes wearing bondage straps, dancing on podiums to throbbing techno. But
this place feels like home to me; my own neighborhood mega-club. So maybe I
can't venture into the exclusive men-only sex club in the basement, and
sure, I'm usually greeted with scowls instead of smiles by the staff, but
that doesn't mean I'm not welcome here. The attitude is just a front; you
can choose to be offended by it or not. If you're looking for artificial
politeness you can go elsewhere - this place is for dancing and forgetting
yourself, not necessarily making one-night friends. (Unless of course it's
one of those one-night friends you can snuggle up to in the darkrooms....)

Things get different as it gets later into the day. After the novices go
home and the sun comes back up, the place turns into a dirty, cracked out
rave. Water bottles start replacing beer bottles as the beverage of choice
on the dancefloor. A boy with silver shoes dances with his eyes closed. A
guy in Madchester-esque overalls holds a sunflower. Couples are making out
in the dark cubbies that line the hallways, as well as in the middle of the
dancefloor. The shutters covering the huge windows quickly open, flashing a
burst of daylight into the dark club, and the crowd cheers,with big smiles
on their faces. Things get really messy. The parties go into the morning,
afternoon, and the next night. You can dance for 24 hours if you want to.

The main dancefloor downstairs is known for it's hard, stripped down techno.
Lots of DJs of different stripes play here, but many of them tend to play
harder stuff, tailored to fit the atmosphere of the club. Upstairs in the
Panorama Bar, the sound is a little lighter, but lately moving away from the
minimal that people have come to expect, and more into deep house territory.
Berlin has its own brand of deep house though; simple, tracky, groovy, and
raw. Unlike the sexy saxophone stuff I used to hate hearing in SF clubs (and
in TV commercials, waiting rooms, department stores...), Berlin's house
still has a distinct techno aesthetic. It's deep house for people who
thought they hated deep house.

I thought I would share a list of some of the tracks I've heard at my
favorite club over the past few months. (Or, rather, the few tracks I can
actually remember)

Soundstream - Live Goes OnWax 10001 (side a)   - - - (These first two tracks
are the biggest Berlin anthems of Fall '08)
Sleeparchive - Bleep 1
Green Velvet - Flash
DHS - House of God (Martin Landsky Remix)
Robin S - Show Me Love
Herbert - Moving Like A Train (Smith N Hack Mix)
Tyche - Scald
Age Of Love - Age Of Love
Cajmere - Brighter Days
Robert Hood - Minus
Candido - Thousand Finger Man


Just wanted to share a little about my experiences as an expat party girl in
the Techno Capital.

Love from Chelsea Faith  <3

Eclektronik Groove w/ Holt Sorenson - Mon 9AM-12PM Pacific/US
--------------------------------------------------------------

Entering it's 16th year, KZSU's Solstice Marathon take over 
the station for 24 hours and bring you the finest dance music
beats with DJs hooking you up from the studios of KZSU with
grooves and music love from across the musical landscape.
It starts in a few hours on Monday December 22nd at Midnight
Pacific.

This event is free and streams online so you can listen to
it from anywhere the internet is online.

Please tune in to KZSU by listening to 90.1 in the Bay Area or
pointing your web browser to http://kzsulive.stanford.edu.

Line up and other information at: http://hsomusic.com/marathon/

myself along with Marc(o) and DJ Zenith this Friday at
Anu for Faktion Parallelisms:
More at: http://hsomusic.com/events/

There is no cover for the event, so stop by and say hello
and wish Marc(o) the best with his 'farewell from the scene'
DJ set.

Epiphany of Sound with J.C. - Th 9AM-12PM Pacific/US
----------------------------------------------------

After 14 years, DJ J.C.'s techno/house/electronica showcase has
garnered much attention and devotion. Like most folks at Stanford's
radio station, he's a volunteer, proving that his motivation isn't
a paycheck; it's his passion to share his interest in one of music's
most eclectic genres. With his conversational style, inclusion of
producers and musicians from both the local & international scene,
and his stewardship of the station's 24-hour marathons during
Solstices and Equinoxes, it's no wonder that DJ J.C has made a
connection with listeners in a very crowded market. Catch his live
broadcasts or listen to the previous week's program at underheard.org.

J.C. will email this week if he has an update on any guests.

Thanks for your support!!!

It's also quite entertaining because it's from Europe, where drug
research isn't quite as propaganda-driven (although I'm sure that
happens as well). And in that the suppressive effect of the MDMA is
lessened by the loud music, although not completely dispelled. I know
people who think of E as a sex drug but I've never had that opinion
myself. This is purely a cultural critic opinion, of course, as I've
never done any drugs myself, and would never be foolish enough to
discuss drug use openly if I had, but given what I've read in books,
it seem as if people who use E think of it as a drug for emotional
intimacy and connection, whereas less-informed people see it as a drug
for physical intimacy, connection, etc. So yeah. Go weird
rat-rave-throwing scientists go. You gotta wonder what these rats
think of these fucking scientists, btw. I bet the rats in these
experiments had an unusually high opinion of the whole lab rat
lifestyle.

'Lust Lounge 08' - December installment for UR MONTHLY DOSE

http://www.waxdj.com/djs/5512

Slowing things down for the holiday season with a Trip Hop, Funk  
infused, Acid Jazz set....  Best enjoyed when you are in a pensive  
state or keeping warm with friends or a special someone.

Complete Track Listing:

Track 1: 'Au Pair Girls' - The Wiseguys
Track 2 @ 5:30: 'Bass And Several Cars' - Shantel
Track 3 @ 7:45: 'Ice is the silent language' - 1000 names
Track 4 @ 9:44: 'Soul Purpose' - Nightmares On Wax
Track 5 @ 13:14: 'A Mother' - Herbalizer
Track 6 @ 17:42: 'Trans Fatty Acid' - Lamb
Track 7 @ 24:42: 'Deep Shit (Pt 1 and 2)' - Kruder and Dorfmeister
Track 8 @ 28:27: 'Fiendish Fifth' - Shawn Lee's Ping Pong Orchestra
Track 9 @ 31:30: 'Transitions' - Beastie Boys
Track 10 @ 33:01: 'Colours Don't Leak' - Kelpe
Track 11 @ 36:02: 'The Sweatest' - Nightmares on Wax
Track 12 @ 41:09: 'Sleepwalk' - Soulstice
Track 13 @ 44:33: 'Find a Way' - Unknown
Track 14 @ 51:17: 'Electric Sunday' - Giano
Track 15 @ 55:39: 'Do Do Wop is Strong in Here' (Ashley Beedle Re- 
edit) - Curtis Mayfield
Track 16 @ 60:20: 'Interlude' - Thievery Corporation
Track 17 @ 62:08: 'Sunset' - Fuku Syndicate
Track 18 @ 67:09: 'You Wish' - Nightmares on Wax

Many of you may not know but I put out a mix the first week of every  
month, MP3 format, generally house music, all shades (UR MONTHLY  
DOSE).  If you would like to receive these mixes as they come out,  
shoot me your email and I'll add you to my mailing list.  Would love  
as many househeads as possible!

'UMD' 2008 archived installments are here --> http://www.jpadilla.net

Don't hesitate to hit me up if you would like to know the name of a  
certain track, comments, etc...

Enjoy and Happy Holidays.

-J Padilla
--Apple-Mail-3-514021191--

Subject: [sfraves] BSP - Subterra NYE @ SomArts

On December 31st, a special collaboration between Tantra,
Know:Audio, and Symbiosis will occur. Last NYE, Resolution 2008
at the SomArts was the place to be on New Years Eve. This year,
with help from our friends Ambient Mafia, Koinonea, and The
Connoisseur Collective, we're going to out-do ourselves in
every way possible. Please note that last year we were filled
to over-capacity. We won't let that happen this year so please
be sure to get your tickets ahead of time. The event not to be
missed this NYE is:


SUBTERRA: New Years Eve 2009


KNOW:AUDIO Techno Room

Worthy (dirtybird)

Subject: [sfraves] [BSP] Faktion Parallelizm/Boxing Day/8 hours/free/26 Dec


Friday, 26 December 2008

R A Y presents:

F A K T I O N : giving the gift of dance

Friday, 26 December 2008
Marco                                                             
Qorser                                                             
Leathal
DJ Zenith                                                           
Holt Sorenson

Thanks to all for an amazing 2008!  To wrap the year, our boxing day party
presents 8 hours of some of the best in west coast talent!  We're proud to
present Marco Mirenzi's retirement appearance, this is scheduled to be his
final set before he hangs up his headphones and says farewell to the dance
scene.  The dynamic duo Leathal, aka Paul and Chris Leath are also in town
to continue the Christmas cheer, along with DJ Zenith, Qorser and Holt
Sorenson.  This will be a FREE party, so come on out and party with all
of us!  Come early, come late, there shall be beats aplenty from 6 to closing.

4th Fridays @ Anu


Anu-Bar 
43 Sixth St., San Francisco, CA
6 PM to 2 AM 21+
Cost: FREE FREE FREE

Official Site: http://www.faktionsf.com/
Official Site: http://www.defsf.com/radiointegrated
